      <p>
       The
       <b>
        World Trade Organization
       </b>
       (
       <b>
        WTO
       </b>
       ) is an
       <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_organization" title="Intergovernmental organization">
        intergovernmental organization
       </a>
       that regulates
       <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">
        international trade
       </a>
       . The WTO officially commenced on 1 January 1995 under the
       <a href="/wiki/Marrakesh_Agreement" title="Marrakesh Agreement">
        Marrakesh Agreement
       </a>
       , signed by 123 nations on 15 April 1994, replacing the
       <a href="/wiki/General_Agreement_on_Tariffs_and_Trade" title="General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade">
        General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade
       </a>
       (GATT), which commenced in 1948. It is the largest international economic organization in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The WTO deals with regulation of trade in goods, services and intellectual property between participating countries by providing a framework for negotiating
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_agreement" title="Trade agreement">
        trade agreements
       </a>
       and a
       <a href="/wiki/Dispute_resolution" title="Dispute resolution">
        dispute resolution
       </a>
       process aimed at enforcing participants' adherence to WTO agreements, which are signed by representatives of member governments
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-underst_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-underst-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         fol.9–10
        </span>
       </sup>
       and ratified by their parliaments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-britannica_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-britannica-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most of the issues that the WTO focuses on derive from previous trade negotiations, especially from the
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_Round" title="Uruguay Round">
        Uruguay Round
       </a>
       (1986–1994).
      </p>
      <p>
       The WTO's current Director-General is
       <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Azev%C3%AAdo" title="Roberto Azevêdo">
        Roberto Azevêdo
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardn_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-guardn-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       who leads a staff of over 600 people in
       <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">
        Geneva
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
        Switzerland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A trade facilitation agreement, part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bali_Package" title="Bali Package">
        Bali Package
       </a>
       of decisions, was agreed by all members on 7 December 2013, the first comprehensive agreement in the organization's history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . On 23 January 2017, the amendment to the WTO Trade Related Aspects of Intellectual Property Rights (TRIPS) Agreement marks the first time since the organization opened its doors in 1995 that WTO accords have been amended, and this change should secure for developing countries a legal pathway to access affordable remedies under WTO rules.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">
         <a href="#History">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           1
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           History
          </span>
         </a>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <div class="floatnone">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Camera-photo.svg" title="link={{{link}}}">
            <img alt="Small camera icon" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/40px-Camera-photo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/60px-Camera-photo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/80px-Camera-photo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>

      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_World_Trade_Organization" title="History of the World Trade Organization">
        History of the World Trade Organization
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WhiteandKeynes.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="630" data-file-width="500" height="277" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/WhiteandKeynes.jpg/220px-WhiteandKeynes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/WhiteandKeynes.jpg/330px-WhiteandKeynes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/WhiteandKeynes.jpg/440px-WhiteandKeynes.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WhiteandKeynes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The economists
         <a href="/wiki/Harry_Dexter_White" title="Harry Dexter White">
          Harry White
         </a>
         (left) and
         <a href="/wiki/John_Maynard_Keynes" title="John Maynard Keynes">
          John Maynard Keynes
         </a>
         at the
         <a href="/wiki/Bretton_Woods_Conference" title="Bretton Woods Conference">
          Bretton Woods Conference
         </a>
         . Both had been strong advocates of a central-controlled international trade environment and recommended the establishment of three institutions: the
         <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
          IMF
         </a>
         (for fiscal and monetary issues); the
         <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">
          World Bank
         </a>
         (for financial and structural issues); and the
         <a href="/wiki/International_Trade_Organization" title="International Trade Organization">
          ITO
         </a>
         (for international economic cooperation).
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
          <a href="#cite_note-15">
           [15]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The WTO's predecessor, the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade (GATT), was established after
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       in the wake of other new multilateral institutions dedicated to international economic cooperation – such as the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">
        World Bank
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">
        International Monetary Fund
       </a>
       . A comparable international institution for trade, named the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Trade_Organization" title="International Trade Organization">
        International Trade Organization
       </a>
       never started as the treaty was not approved by the U.S. and other signatories,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRS-2007-pg_4_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CRS-2007-pg_4-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and so GATT slowly became a de facto international organization.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B81_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-B81-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="GATT_negotiations_before_Uruguay">
        GATT negotiations before Uruguay
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: GATT negotiations before Uruguay">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/General_Agreement_on_Tariffs_and_Trade" title="General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade">
        General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Seven rounds of negotiations occurred under GATT. The first real GATT trade rounds concentrated on further reducing
       <a href="/wiki/Tariff" title="Tariff">
        tariffs
       </a>
       . Then, the
       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Round" title="Kennedy Round">
        Kennedy Round
       </a>
       in the mid-sixties brought about a GATT
       <a href="/wiki/Dumping_(pricing_policy)" title="Dumping (pricing policy)">
        anti-dumping
       </a>
       Agreement and a section on development. The Tokyo Round during the seventies was the first major attempt to tackle trade barriers that do not take the form of tariffs, and to improve the system, adopting a series of agreements on
       <a href="/wiki/Non-tariff_barriers_to_trade" title="Non-tariff barriers to trade">
        non-tariff barriers
       </a>
       , which in some cases interpreted existing GATT rules, and in others broke entirely new ground. Because these
       <a href="/wiki/Plurilateral_agreement" title="Plurilateral agreement">
        plurilateral agreements
       </a>
       were not accepted by the full GATT membership, they were often informally called "codes". Several of these codes were amended in the Uruguay Round, and turned into multilateral commitments accepted by all WTO members. Only four remained plurilateral (those on government procurement, bovine meat, civil aircraft and dairy products), but in 1997 WTO members agreed to terminate the bovine meat and dairy agreements, leaving only two.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GY_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-GY-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite attempts in the mid-1950s and 1960s to create some form of institutional mechanism for international trade, the GATT continued to operate for almost half a century as a semi-institutionalized multilateral treaty regime on a provisional basis.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-F17_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-F17-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Uruguay_Round">
        Uruguay Round
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Uruguay Round">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">

            <img alt="Small camera icon" data-file-height="48" data-file-width="48" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/40px-Camera-photo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/60px-Camera-photo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/80/Camera-photo.svg/80px-Camera-photo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">

          to comply with

          </b>
          for
          <b>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Captions#Succinctness" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Captions">

           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">

             <b>

              <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Picture_tutorial" title="Wikipedia:Picture tutorial">

             <b>

      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_Round" title="Uruguay Round">
        Uruguay Round
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bush_Lula133635.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1685" data-file-width="2598" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Bush_Lula133635.jpg/220px-Bush_Lula133635.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Bush_Lula133635.jpg/330px-Bush_Lula133635.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Bush_Lula133635.jpg/440px-Bush_Lula133635.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bush_Lula133635.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         During the
         <a href="/wiki/Doha_Development_Round" title="Doha Development Round">
          Doha Round
         </a>
         , the
         <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">
          US government
         </a>
         blamed
         <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
          Brazil
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
          India
         </a>
         for being inflexible and the
         <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
          EU
         </a>
         for impeding agricultural imports.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
          <a href="#cite_note-22">
           [22]
          </a>
         </sup>
         The then-
         <a href="/wiki/President_of_Brazil" title="President of Brazil">
          President of Brazil
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Luiz_In%C3%A1cio_Lula_da_Silva" title="Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva">
          Luiz Inácio Lula da Silva
         </a>
         (above right), responded to the criticisms by arguing that progress would only be achieved if the richest countries (especially the US and countries in the EU) made deeper cuts in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agricultural_subsidies" title="Agricultural subsidies">
          agricultural subsidies
         </a>
         and further opened their markets for agricultural goods.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
          <a href="#cite_note-23">
           [23]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Well before GATT's 40th anniversary, its members concluded that the GATT system was straining to adapt to a new
       <a href="/wiki/Globalization" title="Globalization">
        globalizing
       </a>
       world economy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-G4_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-G4-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UR_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UR-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In response to the problems identified in the 1982 Ministerial Declaration (structural deficiencies, spill-over impacts of certain countries' policies on world trade GATT could not manage etc.), the eighth GATT round – known as the Uruguay Round – was launched in September 1986, in
       <a href="/wiki/Punta_del_Este" title="Punta del Este">
        Punta del Este
       </a>
       , Uruguay.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-G4_24-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-G4-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       It was the biggest negotiating mandate on trade ever agreed: the talks were going to extend the trading system into several new areas, notably trade in services and intellectual property, and to reform trade in the sensitive sectors of agriculture and textiles; all the original GATT articles were up for review.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UR_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-UR-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Final Act concluding the Uruguay Round and officially establishing the WTO regime was signed 15 April 1994, during the ministerial meeting at
       <a href="/wiki/Marrakesh" title="Marrakesh">
        Marrakesh
       </a>
       , Morocco, and hence is known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Marrakesh_Agreement" title="Marrakesh Agreement">
        Marrakesh Agreement
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The GATT still exists as the WTO's umbrella treaty for trade in goods, updated as a result of the Uruguay Round negotiations (a distinction is made between
       <i>
        GATT 1994
       </i>
       , the updated parts of GATT, and
       <i>
        GATT 1947
       </i>
       , the original agreement which is still the heart of GATT 1994).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-G4_24-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-G4-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       GATT 1994 is not however the only legally binding agreement included via the Final Act at Marrakesh; a long list of about 60 agreements, annexes, decisions and understandings was adopted. The agreements fall into six main parts, the Agreement Establishing the WTO, the Multilateral Agreements on Trade in Goods,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/General_Agreement_on_Trade_in_Services" title="General Agreement on Trade in Services">
        General Agreement on Trade in Services
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agreement_on_Trade-Related_Aspects_of_Intellectual_Property_Rights" title="Agreement on Trade-Related Aspects of Intellectual Property Rights">
        Agreement on Trade-Related Aspects of Intellectual Property Rights
       </a>
       , Dispute settlement
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and reviews of governments' trade policies
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OL_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-OL-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In terms of the WTO's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO#Principles_of_the_trading_system" title="WTO">
        principle relating to tariff "ceiling-binding" (No. 3)
       </a>
       , the Uruguay Round has been successful in increasing binding commitments by both developed and developing countries, as may be seen in the percentages of tariffs bound before and after the 1986–1994 talks.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PT_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-PT-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ministerial_conferences">
        Ministerial conferences
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Ministerial conferences">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Geneva_Ministerial_Conference_18-20_May_1998_(9305956531).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1416" data-file-width="2128" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Geneva_Ministerial_Conference_18-20_May_1998_%289305956531%29.jpg/220px-Geneva_Ministerial_Conference_18-20_May_1998_%289305956531%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Geneva_Ministerial_Conference_18-20_May_1998_%289305956531%29.jpg/330px-Geneva_Ministerial_Conference_18-20_May_1998_%289305956531%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Geneva_Ministerial_Conference_18-20_May_1998_%289305956531%29.jpg/440px-Geneva_Ministerial_Conference_18-20_May_1998_%289305956531%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Geneva_Ministerial_Conference_18-20_May_1998_(9305956531).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization_Ministerial_Conference_of_1998" title="World Trade Organization Ministerial Conference of 1998">
          World Trade Organization Ministerial Conference of 1998
         </a>
         , in the
         <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Nations" title="Palace of Nations">
          Palace of Nations
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">
          Geneva
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
          Switzerland
         </a>
         ).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The highest decision-making body of the WTO is the
       <a href="/wiki/Ministerial_Conference" title="Ministerial Conference">
        Ministerial Conference
       </a>
       , which usually meets every two years.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It brings together all members of the WTO, all of which are countries or customs unions. The Ministerial Conference can take decisions on all matters under any of the multilateral trade agreements. Some of these such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO_Ministerial_Conference_of_1996" title="WTO Ministerial Conference of 1996">
        inaugural ministerial conference
       </a>
       in Singapore and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO_Ministerial_Conference_of_2003" title="WTO Ministerial Conference of 2003">
        Cancun conference
       </a>
       in 2003
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       involved arguments between developed and developing economies referred to as the "
       <a href="/wiki/Singapore_issues" title="Singapore issues">
        Singapore issues
       </a>
       " such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agricultural_subsidies" title="Agricultural subsidies">
        agricultural subsidies
       </a>
       while others such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO_Ministerial_Conference_of_1999" title="WTO Ministerial Conference of 1999">
        Seattle conference
       </a>
       in 1999 created large demonstrations. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO_Ministerial_Conference_of_2001" title="WTO Ministerial Conference of 2001">
        fourth ministerial conference
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">
        Doha
       </a>
       in 2001 approved China's entry to the WTO and launched the
       <a href="/wiki/Doha_Development_Round" title="Doha Development Round">
        Doha Development Round
       </a>
       which was supplemented by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO_Ministerial_Conference_of_2005" title="WTO Ministerial Conference of 2005">
        sixth WTO ministerial conference
       </a>
       (in
       <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">
        Hong Kong
       </a>
       ) when agricultural export subsidies were agreed to be phased out and adoption of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Everything_but_Arms" title="Everything but Arms">
        Everything but Arms
       </a>
       initiative to phase out tariffs for goods from the Least Developed Countries.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Doha_Round_.28Doha_Agenda.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Doha_Round_(Doha_Agenda)">
        Doha Round (Doha Agenda)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Doha Round (Doha Agenda)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Doha_Development_Round" title="Doha Development Round">
        Doha Development Round
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The WTO launched the current round of negotiations, the
       <a href="/wiki/Doha_Development_Round" title="Doha Development Round">
        Doha Development Round
       </a>
       , at the fourth ministerial conference in
       <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">
        Doha
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">
        Qatar
       </a>
       in November 2001. This was to be an ambitious effort to make globalization more inclusive and help the world's poor, particularly by slashing barriers and subsidies in farming.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ec65_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Ec65-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The initial agenda comprised both further
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trade_liberalization" title="Trade liberalization">
        trade liberalization
       </a>
       and new rule-making, underpinned by commitments to strengthen substantial assistance to developing countries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECdoha_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ECdoha-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Progress stalled after over differences between
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developed_nations" title="Developed nations">
        developed nations
       </a>
       and the major
       <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">
        developing countries
       </a>
       on issues such as industrial tariffs and non tariff barriers to trade
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crs-2_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-crs-2-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       particularly against and between the EU and the US over their maintenance of
       <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_subsidy" title="Agricultural subsidy">
        agricultural subsidies
       </a>
       —seen to operate effectively as trade barriers. Repeated attempts to revive the talks were unsuccessful
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       though the adoption of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bali_Package" title="Bali Package">
        Bali Ministerial Declaration
       </a>
       in 2013
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wtoBali_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wtoBali-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       addressed bureaucratic barriers to commerce
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcBali_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bbcBali-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of June 2012
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , the future of the Doha Round remained uncertain: the work programme lists 21 subjects in which the original deadline of 1 January 2005 was missed, and the round is still incomplete.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The conflict between free trade on industrial goods and services but retention of
       <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">
        protectionism
       </a>
       on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Farm_subsidies" title="Farm subsidies">
        farm subsidies
       </a>
       to domestic
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agricultural_sector" title="Agricultural sector">
        agricultural sector
       </a>
       (requested by
       <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">
        developed countries
       </a>
       ) and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Substantiation" title="Substantiation">
        substantiation
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Fair_trade" title="Fair trade">
        fair trade
       </a>
       on agricultural products (requested by developing countries) remain the major obstacles. This impasse has made it impossible to launch new WTO negotiations beyond the Doha Development Round. As a result, there have been an increasing number of bilateral
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_trade_agreements" title="Free trade agreements">
        free trade agreements
       </a>
       between governments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of July 2012, there were various negotiation groups in the WTO system for the current agricultural trade negotiation which is in the condition of stalemate.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Functions">
        Functions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Functions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Among the various functions of the WTO, these are regarded by analysts as the most important:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        It oversees the implementation, administration and operation of the covered agreements.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iisd-functions_42-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-iisd-functions-42">
          [42]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTOmain-functions_43-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-WTOmain-functions-43">
          [43]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        It provides a forum for negotiations and for settling disputes.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B17_44-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-B17-44">
          [44]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deere_decision-making_45-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Deere_decision-making-45">
          [45]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Additionally, it is WTO's duty to review and propagate the national trade policies, and to ensure the coherence and transparency of trade policies through surveillance in global economic policy-making.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTOmain-functions_43-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-WTOmain-functions-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deere_decision-making_45-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Deere_decision-making-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Another priority of the WTO is the assistance of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Developing_countries" title="Developing countries">
        developing
       </a>
       , least-developed and low-income countries in transition to adjust to WTO rules and disciplines through technical cooperation and training.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AT_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AT-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        The WTO shall facilitate the implementation, administration and operation and further the objectives of this Agreement and of the Multilateral Trade Agreements, and shall also provide the framework for the implementation, administration and operation of the multilateral Trade Agreements.
       </li>
       <li>
        The WTO shall provide the forum for negotiations among its members concerning their multilateral trade relations in matters dealt with under the Agreement in the Annexes to this Agreement.
       </li>
       <li>
        The WTO shall administer the Understanding on Rules and Procedures Governing the Settlement of Disputes.
       </li>
       <li>
        The WTO shall administer Trade Policy Review Mechanism.
       </li>
       <li>
        With a view to achieving greater coherence in global economic policy making, the WTO shall cooperate, as appropriate, with the international Monetary Fund (IMF) and with the International Bank for Reconstruction and Development (IBRD) and its affiliated agencies.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
         <a href="#cite_note-47">
          [47]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       The above five listings are the additional functions of the World Trade Organization. As globalization proceeds in today's society, the necessity of an
       <a href="/wiki/International_Organization" title="International Organization">
        International Organization
       </a>
       to manage the trading systems has been of vital importance. As the trade volume increases, issues such as protectionism, trade barriers, subsidies, violation of intellectual property arise due to the differences in the trading rules of every nation. The World Trade Organization serves as the mediator between the nations when such problems arise. WTO could be referred to as the product of globalization and also as one of the most important organizations in today's globalized society.
      </p>
      <p>
       The WTO is also a centre of economic research and analysis: regular assessments of the global trade picture in its annual publications and research reports on specific topics are produced by the organization.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EA_48-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EA-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Finally, the WTO cooperates closely with the two other components of the Bretton Woods system, the IMF and the World Bank.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B17_44-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-B17-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Principles_of_the_trading_system">
        Principles of the trading system
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Principles of the trading system">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The WTO establishes a framework for trade policies; it does not define or specify outcomes. That is, it is concerned with setting the rules of the trade policy games.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H42_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-H42-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Five principles are of particular importance in understanding both the pre-1994 GATT and the WTO:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        <b>
         Non-discrimination
        </b>
        . It has two major components: the
        <a href="/wiki/Most_favoured_nation" title="Most favoured nation">
         most favoured nation
        </a>
        (MFN) rule, and the
        <a href="/wiki/National_treatment" title="National treatment">
         national treatment
        </a>
        policy. Both are embedded in the main WTO rules on goods, services, and intellectual property, but their precise scope and nature differ across these areas. The MFN rule requires that a WTO member must apply the same conditions on all trade with other WTO members, i.e. a WTO member has to grant the most favourable conditions under which it allows trade in a certain product type to all other WTO members.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H42_49-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-H42-49">
          [49]
         </a>
        </sup>
        "Grant someone a special favour and you have to do the same for all other WTO members."
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PT_30-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-PT-30">
          [30]
         </a>
        </sup>
        National treatment means that imported goods should be treated no less favourably than domestically produced goods (at least after the foreign goods have entered the market) and was introduced to tackle
        <a href="/wiki/Non-tariff_barriers_to_trade" title="Non-tariff barriers to trade">
         non-tariff barriers to trade
        </a>
        (e.g. technical standards, security standards et al. discriminating against imported goods).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H42_49-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-H42-49">
          [49]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Reciprocity
        </b>
        . It reflects both a desire to limit the scope of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_rider_problem" title="Free rider problem">
         free-riding
        </a>
        that may arise because of the MFN rule, and a desire to obtain better access to foreign markets. A related point is that for a nation to negotiate, it is necessary that the gain from doing so be greater than the gain available from
        <a href="/wiki/Unilateralism" title="Unilateralism">
         unilateral
        </a>
        liberalization; reciprocal concessions intend to ensure that such gains will materialise.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H43_50-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-H43-50">
          [50]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Binding and enforceable commitments
        </b>
        . The tariff commitments made by WTO members in a multilateral trade negotiation and on accession are enumerated in a schedule (list) of concessions. These schedules establish "ceiling bindings": a country can change its bindings, but only after negotiating with its trading partners, which could mean compensating them for loss of trade. If satisfaction is not obtained, the complaining country may invoke the WTO dispute settlement procedures.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PT_30-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-PT-30">
          [30]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H43_50-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-H43-50">
          [50]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Transparency
        </b>
        . The WTO members are required to publish their trade regulations, to maintain institutions allowing for the review of administrative decisions affecting trade, to respond to requests for information by other members, and to notify changes in trade policies to the WTO. These internal transparency requirements are supplemented and facilitated by periodic country-specific reports (trade policy reviews) through the Trade Policy Review Mechanism (TPRM).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H44_51-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-H44-51">
          [51]
         </a>
        </sup>
        The WTO system tries also to improve predictability and stability, discouraging the use of
        <a href="/wiki/Import_quota" title="Import quota">
         quotas
        </a>
        and other measures used to set limits on quantities of imports.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PT_30-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-PT-30">
          [30]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <b>
         Safety values
        </b>
        . In specific circumstances, governments are able to
        <a href="/wiki/Trade_restriction" title="Trade restriction">
         restrict trade
        </a>
        . The WTO's agreements permit members to take measures to protect not only the environment but also public health, animal health and plant health.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wto.org_52-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-wto.org-52">
          [52]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       There are three types of provision in this direction:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        articles allowing for the use of trade measures to attain non-economic objectives;
       </li>
       <li>
        articles aimed at ensuring "fair competition"; members must not use environmental protection measures as a means of disguising protectionist policies.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wto.org_52-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-wto.org-52">
          [52]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
         <a href="#cite_note-53">
          [53]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        provisions permitting intervention in trade for economic reasons.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-H44_51-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-H44-51">
          [51]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       Exceptions to the MFN principle also allow for preferential treatment of
       <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">
        developing countries
       </a>
       , regional
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_trade_area" title="Free trade area">
        free trade areas
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Customs_union" title="Customs union">
        customs unions
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-underst_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-underst-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        :
        <span>
         fol.93
        </span>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Organizational_structure">
        Organizational structure
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Organizational structure">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The General Council has the following subsidiary bodies which oversee committees in different areas:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Council for Trade in Goods
       </dt>
       <dd>
        There are 11 committees under the jurisdiction of the Goods Council each with a specific task. All members of the WTO participate in the committees. The Textiles Monitoring Body is separate from the other committees but still under the jurisdiction of Goods Council. The body has its own chairman and only 10 members. The body also has several groups relating to textiles.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTO_subsidiary_bodies_54-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-WTO_subsidiary_bodies-54">
          [54]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Council for Trade-Related Aspects of Intellectual Property Rights
       </dt>
       <dd>
        Information on intellectual property in the WTO, news and official records of the activities of the TRIPS Council, and details of the WTO's work with other international organizations in the field.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
         <a href="#cite_note-55">
          [55]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Council for Trade in Services
       </dt>
       <dd>
        The Council for Trade in Services operates under the guidance of the General Council and is responsible for overseeing the functioning of the
        <a href="/wiki/General_Agreement_on_Trade_in_Services" title="General Agreement on Trade in Services">
         General Agreement on Trade in Services
        </a>
        (GATS). It is open to all WTO members, and can create subsidiary bodies as required.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTO-Services_council_56-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-WTO-Services_council-56">
          [56]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Trade Negotiations Committee
       </dt>
       <dd>
        The Trade Negotiations Committee (TNC) is the committee that deals with the current trade talks round. The chair is WTO's director-general. As of June 2012
        <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit">
          [update]
         </a>
        </sup>
        the committee was tasked with the
        <a href="/wiki/Doha_Development_Round" title="Doha Development Round">
         Doha Development Round
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTO-TNC_57-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-WTO-TNC-57">
          [57]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The Service Council has three subsidiary bodies: financial services, domestic regulations, GATS rules and specific commitments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTO_subsidiary_bodies_54-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-WTO_subsidiary_bodies-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The council has several different committees, working groups, and working parties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WTO-chart_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WTO-chart-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are committees on the following: Trade and Environment; Trade and Development (Subcommittee on
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Least_developed_country" title="Least developed country">
        Least-Developed Countries
       </a>
       );
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_Trade_Agreement" title="Regional Trade Agreement">
        Regional Trade Agreements
       </a>
       ; Balance of Payments Restrictions; and Budget, Finance and Administration. There are working parties on the following: Accession. There are working groups on the following: Trade, debt and finance; and Trade and technology transfer.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Decision-making">
        Decision-making
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Decision-making">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The WTO describes itself as "a rules-based, member-driven organization—all decisions are made by the member governments, and the rules are the outcome of negotiations among members".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The WTO Agreement foresees votes where consensus cannot be reached, but the practice of consensus dominates the process of decision-making.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Harold_Steinberg" title="Richard Harold Steinberg">
        Richard Harold Steinberg
       </a>
       (2002) argues that although the WTO's consensus governance model provides law-based initial bargaining, trading rounds close through power-based bargaining favouring Europe and the U.S., and may not lead to
       <a href="/wiki/Pareto_efficiency" title="Pareto efficiency">
        Pareto improvement
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dispute_settlement">
        Dispute settlement
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Dispute settlement">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dispute_settlement_in_the_WTO" title="Dispute settlement in the WTO">
        Dispute settlement in the WTO
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The WTO's dispute-settlement system "is the result of the evolution of rules, procedures and practices developed over almost half a century under the GATT 1947".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1994, the WTO members agreed on the Understanding on Rules and Procedures Governing the Settlement of Disputes (DSU) annexed to the "Final Act" signed in Marrakesh in 1994.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dispute settlement is regarded by the WTO as the central pillar of the multilateral trading system, and as a "unique contribution to the stability of the global economy".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       WTO members have agreed that, if they believe fellow-members are violating trade rules, they will use the multilateral system of settling disputes instead of taking action unilaterally.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UnSD_65-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-UnSD-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The operation of the WTO dispute settlement process involves case-specific panels
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       appointed by the Dispute Settlement Body (DSB),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the Appellate Body,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Director-General and the WTO Secretariat,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       arbitrators,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and advisory experts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The priority is to settle disputes, preferably through a mutually agreed solution, and provision has been made for the process to be conducted in an efficient and timely manner so that "If a case is adjudicated, it should normally take no more than one year for a panel ruling and no more than 16 months if the case is appealed... If the complainant deems the case urgent, consideration of the case should take even less time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       WTO member nations are obliged to accept the process as exclusive and compulsory.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Accession_and_membership">
        Accession and membership
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Accession and membership">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization_accession_and_membership" title="World Trade Organization accession and membership">
        World Trade Organization accession and membership
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The process of becoming a WTO member is unique to each applicant country, and the terms of accession are dependent upon the country's stage of economic development and current trade regime.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AS_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AS-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The process takes about five years, on average, but it can last longer if the country is less than fully committed to the process or if political issues interfere. The shortest accession negotiation was that of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kyrgyz_Republic" title="Kyrgyz Republic">
        Kyrgyz Republic
       </a>
       , while the longest was that of Russia, which, having first applied to join GATT in 1993, was approved for membership in December 2011 and became a WTO member on 22 August 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rusmem_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-rusmem-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Kazakhstan also had a long accession negotiation process. The Working Party on the Accession of
       <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">
        Kazakhstan
       </a>
       was established in 1996 and was approved for membership in 2015.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The second longest was that of Vanuatu, whose Working Party on the Accession of Vanuatu was established on 11 July 1995. After a final meeting of the Working Party in October 2001, Vanuatu requested more time to consider its accession terms. In 2008, it indicated its interest to resume and conclude its WTO accession. The Working Party on the Accession of Vanuatu was reconvened informally on 4 April 2011 to discuss Vanuatu's future WTO membership. The re-convened Working Party completed its mandate on 2 May 2011. The General Council formally approved the Accession Package of Vanuatu on 26 October 2011. On 24 August 2012, the WTO welcomed Vanuatu as its 157th member.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       An offer of accession is only given once consensus is reached among interested parties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M64_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-M64-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A 2017 study argues that "political ties rather than issue-area functional gains determine who joins" and shows "how geopolitical alignment shapes the demand and supply sides of membership".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The "findings challenge the view that states first liberalize trade to join the GATT/WTO. Instead, democracy and foreign policy similarity encourage states to join."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_79-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-:0-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Accession_process">
        Accession process
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Accession process">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WTO_enlargement.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="863" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/WTO_enlargement.svg/400px-WTO_enlargement.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/WTO_enlargement.svg/600px-WTO_enlargement.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/WTO_enlargement.svg/800px-WTO_enlargement.svg.png 2x" width="400"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WTO_enlargement.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         WTO accession progress:
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
          <a href="#cite_note-80">
           [80]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #008000; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Draft Working Party Report or Factual Summary adopted
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000ff; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Goods or Services offers submitted
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #eeee00; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Working party meetings
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Memorandum on Foreign Trade Regime submitted
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #ff1111; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Working party established
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       A country wishing to accede to the WTO submits an application to the General Council, and has to describe all aspects of its trade and economic policies that have a bearing on WTO agreements.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BM_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BM-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The application is submitted to the WTO in a
       <a href="/wiki/Memorandum" title="Memorandum">
        memorandum
       </a>
       which is examined by a working party open to all interested WTO Members.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After all necessary background information has been acquired, the working party focuses on issues of discrepancy between the WTO rules and the applicant's international and domestic trade policies and laws. The working party determines the terms and conditions of entry into the WTO for the applicant nation, and may consider transitional periods to allow countries some leeway in complying with the WTO rules.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AS_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-AS-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The final phase of accession involves bilateral negotiations between the applicant nation and other working party members regarding the concessions and commitments on tariff levels and market access for goods and services. The new member's commitments are to apply equally to all WTO members under normal non-discrimination rules, even though they are negotiated bilaterally.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BM_81-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-BM-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       When the bilateral talks conclude, the working party sends to the general council or ministerial conference an accession package, which includes a summary of all the working party meetings, the Protocol of Accession (a draft membership treaty), and lists ("schedules") of the member-to-be's commitments. Once the general council or ministerial conference approves of the terms of accession, the applicant's parliament must ratify the Protocol of Accession before it can become a member.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some countries may have faced tougher and a much longer accession process due to challenges during negotiations with other WTO members, such as Vietnam, whose negotiations took more than 11 years before it became official member in January 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Members_and_observers">
        Members and observers
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Members and observers">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The WTO has 164 members and 23 observer governments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-memberlist_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-memberlist-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Liberia became the 163rd member on 14 July 2016, and Afghanistan became the 164th member on 29 July 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In addition to states, the European Union, and each EU Country in its own right,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is a member. WTO members do not have to be fully independent states; they need only be a customs territory with full autonomy in the conduct of their external commercial relations. Thus Hong Kong has been a member since 1995 (as "Hong Kong, China" since 1997) predating the People's Republic of China, which joined in 2001 after 15 years of negotiations. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" title="Republic of China">
        Republic of China
       </a>
       (Taiwan) acceded to the WTO in 2002 as "Separate Customs Territory of China:
       <a href="/wiki/Taiwan" title="Taiwan">
        Taiwan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Penghu" title="Penghu">
        Penghu
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kinmen" title="Kinmen">
        Kinmen
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Matsu_Islands" title="Matsu Islands">
        Matsu
       </a>
       " (
       <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Taipei" title="Chinese Taipei">
        Chinese Taipei
       </a>
       ) despite its
       <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">
        disputed status
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J109_89-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-J109-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The WTO Secretariat omits the official titles (such as Counsellor, First Secretary, Second Secretary and Third Secretary) of the members of Chinese Taipei's Permanent Mission to the WTO, except for the titles of the Permanent Representative and the Deputy Permanent Representative.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of 2007, WTO member states represented 96.4% of global trade and 96.7% of global GDP.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">
        Iran
       </a>
       , followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
        Algeria
       </a>
       , are the economies with the largest GDP and trade outside the WTO, using 2005 data.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With the exception of the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">
        Holy See
       </a>
       , observers must start accession negotiations within five years of becoming observers. A number of international intergovernmental organizations have also been granted observer status to WTO bodies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       12
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_member_states" title="UN member states">
        UN member states
       </a>
       have no official affiliation with the WTO.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Agreements">
        Agreements
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Agreements">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_Round" title="Uruguay Round">
        Uruguay Round
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The WTO oversees about 60 different agreements which have the status of international legal texts. Member countries must sign and ratify all WTO agreements on accession.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A discussion of some of the most important agreements follows.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Agreement_on_Agriculture" title="Agreement on Agriculture">
        Agreement on Agriculture
       </a>
       came into effect with the establishment of the WTO at the beginning of 1995. The AoA has three central concepts, or "pillars": domestic support,
       <a href="/wiki/Market_access" title="Market access">
        market access
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Export_subsidies" title="Export subsidies">
        export subsidies
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/General_Agreement_on_Trade_in_Services" title="General Agreement on Trade in Services">
        General Agreement on Trade in Services
       </a>
       was created to extend the multilateral trading system to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_industry" title="Tertiary sector of industry">
        service sector
       </a>
       , in the same way as the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade (GATT) provided such a system for merchandise trade. The agreement entered into force in January 1995.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agreement_on_Trade-Related_Aspects_of_Intellectual_Property_Rights" title="Agreement on Trade-Related Aspects of Intellectual Property Rights">
        Agreement on Trade-Related Aspects of Intellectual Property Rights
       </a>
       sets down minimum standards for many forms of intellectual property (IP) regulation. It was negotiated at the end of the Uruguay Round of the General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade (GATT) in 1994.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Agreement_on_the_Application_of_Sanitary_and_Phytosanitary_Measures" title="Agreement on the Application of Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures">
        Agreement on the Application of Sanitary and Phytosanitary Measures
       </a>
       —also known as the SPS Agreement—was negotiated during the
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_Round" title="Uruguay Round">
        Uruguay Round
       </a>
       of GATT, and entered into force with the establishment of the WTO at the beginning of 1995. Under the SPS agreement, the WTO sets constraints on members' policies relating to food safety (bacterial contaminants, pesticides, inspection and labelling) as well as animal and plant health (imported pests and diseases).
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Agreement_on_Technical_Barriers_to_Trade" title="Agreement on Technical Barriers to Trade">
        Agreement on Technical Barriers to Trade
       </a>
       is an international
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty" title="Treaty">
        treaty
       </a>
       of the World Trade Organization. It was negotiated during the
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_Round" title="Uruguay Round">
        Uruguay Round
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/General_Agreement_on_Tariffs_and_Trade" title="General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade">
        General Agreement on Tariffs and Trade
       </a>
       , and entered into force with the establishment of the WTO at the end of 1994. The object ensures that technical negotiations and standards, as well as testing and certification procedures, do not create unnecessary obstacles to trade".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO_Agreement_on_Customs_Valuation" title="WTO Agreement on Customs Valuation">
        Agreement on Customs Valuation
       </a>
       , formally known as the Agreement on Implementation of Article VII of GATT, prescribes methods of customs valuation that Members are to follow. Chiefly, it adopts the "transaction value" approach.
      </p>
      <p>
       In December 2013, the biggest agreement within the WTO was signed and known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Bali_Package" title="Bali Package">
        Bali Package
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Global_Trade_Deal_Reached_98-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Global_Trade_Deal_Reached-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Office_of_director-general">
        Office of director-general
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Office of director-general">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cwr_lake_facade2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="400" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Cwr_lake_facade2.jpg/220px-Cwr_lake_facade2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Cwr_lake_facade2.jpg/330px-Cwr_lake_facade2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/Cwr_lake_facade2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cwr_lake_facade2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The headquarters of the World Trade Organization in
         <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">
          Geneva
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">
          Switzerland
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The procedures for the appointment of the WTO director-general were published in January 2003.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additionally, there are four deputy directors-general. As of 1 October 2017
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=World_Trade_Organization&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       , under director-general Roberto Azevêdo, the four deputy directors-general are Yi Xiaozhun of China, Karl-Ernst Brauner of Germany, Yonov Frederick Agah of Nigeria and Alan W. Wolff of the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

           <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=The+World+Trade+Organization%3A+Background+and+Issues&amp;rft.pages=4&amp;rft.pub=Congressional+Research+Service&amp;rft.date=2007-05-09&amp;rft.aulast=Fergusson&amp;rft.aufirst=Ian+F.&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.nationalaglawcenter.org%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2Fassets%2Fcrs%2F98-928.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWorld+Trade+Organization">

         <li id="cite_note-B81-19">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-B81_19-0">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           It was contemplated that the GATT would be applied for several years until the ITO came into force. However, since the ITO was never brought into being, the GATT gradually became the focus for international governmental cooperation on trade matters with economist Nicholas Halford overseeing the implementation of GATT in members policies. (P. van den Bossche,
           <i>
            The Law and Policy of the World Trade Organization
           </i>
           , 81; J.H. Jackson,
           <i>
            Managing the Trading System
           </i>
           , 134).
